  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2804241e-e36b-47ee-bd45-26c85aaf5ba7'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText7429802046310095273" style="display:none"><i>Love speaks in flowers. Truth requires thorns.</i><br /><br />Travel to a world of dark bargains struck by moonlight, of haunted towns and hungry woods, of talking beasts and gingerbread golems, where a young mermaid's voice can summon deadly storms and where a river might do a lovestruck boy's bidding but only for a terrible price.<br /><br />Inspired by myth, fairy tale, and folklore, #1 New York Times–bestselling author Leigh Bardugo has crafted a deliciously atmospheric collection of short stories filled with betrayals, revenge, sacrifice, and love.<br /><br />Perfect for new readers and dedicated fans, these tales will transport you to lands both familiar and strange—to a fully realized world of dangerous magic that millions have visited through the novels of the Grishaverse.<br /><br />This collection of six stories includes three brand-new tales, all of them lavishly illustrated with art that changes with each turn of the page, culminating in six stunning full-spread illustrations as rich in detail as the stories themselves.</span>

<div id="review_1911274944" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1911274944" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1911274944?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1911274944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10031552753908119172"><blockquote>
  <i>So shut the window tight and make sure the latch is fastened. Dark things have a way of slipping in through narrow spaces.</i>
</blockquote><br/>*shivers*<br/><br/>Bardugo is definitely at her best when writing short stories. These <b>dark, haunting and beautifully-written</b> little fairy tales had me reading at every spare moment. They have that timeless fairy tale quality, reminiscent of Neil Gaiman and Laini Taylor’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6369113.Lips_Touch_Three_Times' title='Lips Touch Three Times by Laini Taylor' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lips Touch: Three Times</a>. And if you’re considering whether it is worth buying a hardcover copy of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34076952.The_Language_of_Thorns_Midnight_Tales_and_Dangerous_Magic' title='The Language of Thorns Midnight Tales and Dangerous Magic by Leigh Bardugo' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Language </a></span>
  <span id="freeText10031552753908119172" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>So shut the window tight and make sure the latch is fastened. Dark things have a way of slipping in through narrow spaces.</i>
</blockquote><br />*shivers*<br /><br />Bardugo is definitely at her best when writing short stories. These <b>dark, haunting and beautifully-written</b> little fairy tales had me reading at every spare moment. They have that timeless fairy tale quality, reminiscent of Neil Gaiman and Laini Taylor’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6369113.Lips_Touch_Three_Times" title="Lips Touch Three Times by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Lips Touch: Three Times</a>. And if you’re considering whether it is worth buying a hardcover copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34076952.The_Language_of_Thorns_Midnight_Tales_and_Dangerous_Magic" title="The Language of Thorns Midnight Tales and Dangerous Magic by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">The Language of Thorns</a> - definitely go for it. It is STUNNING.<br /><br />I actually wasn’t aware that three of the stories are ones that were available online beforehand and that I had read already - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17790188.The_Too_Clever_Fox__The_Grisha___2_5_" title="The Too-Clever Fox (The Grisha, #2.5) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">The Too-Clever Fox</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13643163.The_Witch_of_Duva__The_Grisha___0_5_" title="The Witch of Duva (The Grisha, #0.5) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">The Witch of Duva</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20818790.Little_Knife__The_Grisha___2_6_" title="Little Knife (The Grisha, #2.6) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Knife</a> - but I also don’t care that much because they are all fantastic and I read them again just to see them play out alongside the gorgeous illustrations.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“This goes to show you that sometimes the unseen is not to be feared and that those meant to love us most are not always the ones who do.”</i>
</blockquote><br />All of these stories take inspiration from classic fairy tales, but I wouldn’t really call them retellings (except maybe the last one - <i>When Water Sang Fire</i>). Bardugo tells brand new stories with nods to the classics, such as <i>The Little Mermaid</i> and <i>Hansel and Gretel</i>, often leaving us with a very different ending or message than what we would have expected.<br /><br />As she notes in the afterword, many fairy tales feature characters completing impossible tasks to win love or acceptance, but this has always felt... <b>wrong</b> somehow. Much of Bardugo’s work here is guided by a sense of dissatisfaction with traditional fairy tales; a sense that maybe the villains were not who we first thought, and that maybe the love of a handsome prince isn’t everything. <br /><br /><b>It is freaking fantastic for twisted, unromantic minds like mine.</b> It is so satisfying to have my expectations shattered; to read sentences like the following and smile because I know, I just <i>know</i>, that it’s about to be torn to shreds:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Come now, Ayama. You know how the stories go. Interesting things only happen to pretty girls;”</i>
</blockquote><br />I recommend this for anyone who enjoys fairy tale-style stories and/or retellings, regardless of whether you usually enjoy Bardugo’s books or not. I get a completely different vibe from her short stories and they are nothing like the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__Shadow_and_Bone___1_" title="Shadow and Bone (Shadow and Bone, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a> trilogy or the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23437156.Six_of_Crows__Six_of_Crows___1_" title="Six of Crows (Six of Crows, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a> duology. I would be happy if she just kept releasing short story collections and forgot about the novels, to be honest.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10031552753908119172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1898623917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer935849659389445312">THIS WAS SO GOOD AND I'M NOT SURPRISED AT ALL ABOUT IT<br/>This was delightfully dark and creepy and was the perfect fairy tale collection for a universe I have come to love. Leigh Bardugo is not only incredible at writing novels, she also writes outstanding shorter pieces. Her writing style is perfect for fairy tales. I'M OBSESSED. <br/><br/>Also THE ILLUSTRATIONS oh my goodness I could not stop marvelling at them and how they formed a frame around the pages and something was added every time you flipped the </span>
  <span id="freeText935849659389445312" style="display:none">THIS WAS SO GOOD AND I'M NOT SURPRISED AT ALL ABOUT IT<br />This was delightfully dark and creepy and was the perfect fairy tale collection for a universe I have come to love. Leigh Bardugo is not only incredible at writing novels, she also writes outstanding shorter pieces. Her writing style is perfect for fairy tales. I'M OBSESSED. <br /><br />Also THE ILLUSTRATIONS oh my goodness I could not stop marvelling at them and how they formed a frame around the pages and something was added every time you flipped the page until the story was complete. It made for such an enhanced reading experience. <br /><br />All of these tales are 5/5 stars honestly, but here they are in order of favourite to least favourite. <br /><br />1. The Too-Clever Fox<br />2. The Soldier Prince<br />3. The Witch of Duva<br />4. Ayama and the Thorn Wood<br />5. When Water Sang Fire<br />6. Little Knife (this one actually might be closer to 4/5 stars, it was kind of boring)<br /><br />For any fan of the grishaverse, this is a MUST read IMO. Whenever you read it, doesn't matter, just do it (personally I would read it after having read at least one of the books set in this universe, so then you're already familiar with the world and this just enhances your understanding).</span>

<div id="review_1970126138" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1970126138" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1970126138?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=novellas-and-short-stories">novellas-and-short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=subscription-box-fairyloot">subscription-box-fairyloot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=anthologies">anthologies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1970126138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2813163663601109253"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507596880i/24130720._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>The Language of Thorns: Midnight Tales and Dangerous Magic</i> is a bind up of six fairy tales that take place in the Grishaverse, which is the same world that her <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1386025950' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadow and Bone series</a> and her <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1441209304?book_show_action=falses' rel='nofollow noopener'>Six of Crows series</a> take place! All of these are expertly crafted. All of these are so very lyrical and beautiful. All of these feel powerful and impactful. All of these are absolutely haunting. <br/><br/>And only Leigh Bardugo could bring me to tears while reading the sentence <i>“I hope you stir the pot.”</i><br/><br/>These stories </span>
  <span id="freeText2813163663601109253" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507596880i/24130720._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>The Language of Thorns: Midnight Tales and Dangerous Magic</i> is a bind up of six fairy tales that take place in the Grishaverse, which is the same world that her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1386025950" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone series</a> and her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1441209304?book_show_action=falses" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows series</a> take place! All of these are expertly crafted. All of these are so very lyrical and beautiful. All of these feel powerful and impactful. All of these are absolutely haunting. <br><br>And only Leigh Bardugo could bring me to tears while reading the sentence <i>“I hope you stir the pot.”</i><br><br>These stories are also illustrated and Sara Kipin's art took my breath away. This whole book is a gorgeous masterpiece from the dust-jacket, to the cover, to the spine, to the art that progresses throughout the story that eventually leads to full-page beautiful artwork, to Leigh’s perfect writing that will make you evoke every emotion ever felt. This is easily one of the top books published in 2017. <br><br>And my personal favorite in the whole collection, which moved me to a whole hot mess of tears, was <i>When Water Sand Fire </i>. If you can only read one of these amazing stories, please pick that one. It’s the longest, but the most fulfilling, and hopefully is the start of something beautiful. <br> <br>I'm going to break down each short story with my thoughts, opinions, and individual star rating!<br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Ayama and the Thorn Wood</b>
</u> - ★★★★★<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“This goes to show you that sometimes the unseen is not to be feared and that those meant to love us most are not always the ones who do.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This story was actually heartbreakingly perfect. It surrounds a small kingdom, where the king and his wife have given birth to two sons, one that is loved and one that is not because of the way he looks. Meanwhile, a young girl in the village is treated like a servant to her family that only sees her beautiful sister. Their paths cross, and continue to cross, because everyone in the village believe both of them to be expendable just based on their appearance, but together they forge something more beautiful than eyes can see and together they can change the kingdom. And they teach that kingdom that the world can be so much more beautiful when you stop only looking physically. <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>The Too-Clever Fox</b>
</u> - ★★★★<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I can bear ugliness,” he said. “I find the one thing I cannot live with is death.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This is such a beautiful story about perspective and how we are never as smart as we feel we are. Also, sometimes being smart has nothing to do with knowledge, but completely with the actions you take. This story centers around the cleverest fox in all of Ravka. From birth, he has been at a disadvantage because of his looks, but he compensates by being a witty and clever trickster. Also, this story reads so much like an actual fairy tale story that we would read in our world, even. <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>The Witch of Duva</b>
</u> - ★★★★★<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There was a time when the woods near Duva ate girls.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>You can actually read this short story for free <a href="https://www.tor.com/2012/06/06/the-witch-of-duva-a-ravkan-folk-tale/" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a> thanks to Tor! And I can’t recommend you read it enough, because this short story actually shook my entire world. This is such a perfectly woven and absolutely haunting tale about a village who is mourning their lost girls, while also trying to endure very hard winters. And the ending of this story is beyond words, and turned me into a crying, melted, weeping, puddle on the floor. Also, this one should probably have a few trigger warnings for abuse (physical/sexual) and just violence in general, even though these things are very vague in the story they are still there, just woven in quietly. <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Little Knife</b>
</u> - ★★★★<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It is dangerous to travel the northern road with a troubled heart.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This is a lovely tale about beauty and owing it to no one but yourself. This is also a tale about never underestimating what greedy men will do for things they feel they are entitled to. This story actually reminded me very much of my favorite saint, Rose of Lima, and her life and the consequences of being so beautiful. And an unexpected love story will always be the best love story. <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>The Soldier Prince</b>
</u> - ★★★★<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“This is the problem with even lesser demons. They come to your doorstep in velvet coats and polished shoes. They tip their hats and smile and demonstrate good table manners. They never show you their tails.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Give me all of the Ketterdam tales, please. And this was a super twisted, yet amazing, retelling of <i>The Nutcracker</i>. And Leigh perfectly mixes what you would expect from a mash up of <i>The Nutcracker</i> and the streets of Ketterdam. And Droessen might be the best character debut in this entire short story collection. Like, I’d love a full-length novel just about him and his entire backstory. But yeah, this is such a creepy little tale that I really enjoyed. <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>When Water Sand Fire</b>
</u> - ★★★★★<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“This is the problem with making a thing forbidden. It does nothing but build an ache in the heart.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Be still, my everything. This story. Lord, this story. This story gave me life. This short story was so perfectly crafted and the tale was so perfectly woven into a simple masterpiece. This was easily my favorite story in the entire collection. Also, this is the story that features one of the best characters ever written in modern day literature, the Darkling. This story surrounds two girls who live under the sea. One is ostracized for being different, and the other is forced to sing alongside her, but when they sing they’re more magical than any other singing group. After a turn of events, they are taken above the sea where magic grants them legs to walk among humans. But soon our main character, Ulla, realizes the heart of sea folk isn’t much different than the heart of men. And that pain and hatred can find a way inside of all of our hearts, if we let it. And I just am praying with all of my soul and with the entirety of who I am that we will cross paths with Ulla again in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2135722641" rel="nofollow noopener">King of Scars</a>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I was not made to please princes.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I gave <i>The Language of Thorns</i> five stars overall, because out of a possible 30 stars (5 stars possible for each of the 6 stories) this collection accumulated 27 stars <b>(90%)</b>. But, like, throw away all of those stars, because this book is one of the best things that 2017 has produced. It’s beautiful, detailed, thoughtful, whimsical, and every single thing I look for in good fairy tales. I can’t recommend this masterpiece enough.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507596880i/24130719._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2813163663601109253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2141265782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7361444417700092035"><b>I think I just fell into the DARK WITCH'S WOOD OF MAGIC and I am literally bursting with love.</b> Like please just insert ALL the heart-eye emojis here. What is this magical thing?!? I was smitten, I tell you. And plus the bookish-inception isn't lost on me ok. This is like a story within a story.<br/><br/>Why must the Grishaverse be so AMAZING. I want 9.<br/><br/><b>All the fairy tales have faint resemblance to ones I know!</b> Like I could see Little Mermaid influences and the Nutcracker and Hansel and Gretel. But they're </span>
  <span id="freeText7361444417700092035" style="display:none"><b>I think I just fell into the DARK WITCH'S WOOD OF MAGIC and I am literally bursting with love.</b> Like please just insert ALL the heart-eye emojis here. What is this magical thing?!? I was smitten, I tell you. And plus the bookish-inception isn't lost on me ok. This is like a story within a story.<br /><br />Why must the Grishaverse be so AMAZING. I want 9.<br /><br /><b>All the fairy tales have faint resemblance to ones I know!</b> Like I could see Little Mermaid influences and the Nutcracker and Hansel and Gretel. But they're wayyyyy way different and DARK. And super super dark at times. <b>And the best part?!? They were loaded with plot twists.</b> It was like ever dumb fairy tale trope just got kicked in the teeth. We don't throw princesses into the arms of the first prince they meet. Beauty isn't everything. Princes suck. The beast is sweet. Here is the sea witch's origin story. The dark woods are not the <i>only</i> problem here. <b>It captivated me on EVERY page with how amazing it was.</b> And detailed!! And clever!! This book is literally the most clever thing.<br /><br /><b>And there's SO much food in here.</b> I pretty much wanted to eat my copy.<br /><br /><b>And it's frikkin' gorgeous.</b> Petition for all books of ever to be illustrated. That would be nice. I ADORED the artwork on every page and the double-page spreads were just...ugh my eyeballs just ran off with this book and married it at dawn.<br /><br /><b>These are like fairy tales as they SHOULD be.</b> Dark and feminist. Yes please. And like full cheers for having women be evil AND good AND clever AND complex. There's monsters and wooden dolls with identity crises and queer girls and endless endless magic that just inspires me. I seriously feel so FULL of magic right now. I could got eat a moon or write a book or, like, eat a pie. Options.</span>

<div id="review_1897509185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1897509185" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1897509185?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=gorgeous-writing">gorgeous-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=she-did-that">she-did-that</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=plot-twists">plot-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=romance-free">romance-free</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=trope-subversion">trope-subversion</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1897509185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14949311118799916139"><b>
  <u>These are so, so utterly beautiful.</u>
</b><br/><br/>I have not actually read the Grisha Trilogy [okay. now I have.], only Six of Crows, but Bardugo's attention to detail in planning her Grisha world comes through in every one of her books that I've read. This one is no exception. Somehow, <b>these stories are more than just folktales;</b> they feel both like folktales told by your grandmother and ghost stories told by your friend beside a campfire. <br/><blockquote>
<i>It wasn't the cannibal witch that bothered me. It wasn't even the </i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14949311118799916139" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>These are so, so utterly beautiful.</u>
</b><br><br>I have not actually read the Grisha Trilogy [okay. now I have.], only Six of Crows, but Bardugo's attention to detail in planning her Grisha world comes through in every one of her books that I've read. This one is no exception. Somehow, <b>these stories are more than just folktales;</b> they feel both like folktales told by your grandmother and ghost stories told by your friend beside a campfire. <br><blockquote>
<i>It wasn't the cannibal witch that bothered me. It wasn't even the selfish stepmother. For me, the real villain was Hansel and Gretel's father, a man so weak-willed, so cowardly, that he let his wicked wife send the children into the woods to die not once but twice.</i> Don't go back,<i> I would whisper as we approached the inevitable final illustration—happy father reunited with children, evil stepmother banished—and I was always left with a feeling of unease as I turned the last page.</i>
</blockquote><br>Above all, this collection subverts its source material in ways clever and creative and, always, compelling. <b>If you're a fan of trope subversion, you'll love this.</b><br><br>Also, please just look at the art. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/misc/1502122860-1502122860_goodreads_misc.jpg" width="500" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>// THE STORY REVIEWS</b><br><br><i># Ayama and the Thorn Wood</i> - ★★★★★<br>This is like a mashup of Cinderella and Beauty &amp; the Beast. It's a story about the power of being heard in a world that wants to shut your voice off. It's brilliant, and all the stories within are even more so. <br><br><i># The Too-Clever Fox</i> - ★★★★☆<br>I can't believe a story this short managed to make my spine tingle. Here, Bardugo tells the story of a clever fox and a hunter who is just as clever. This novella reads exactly like a word-of-mouth-tale, with an archetypal trickster character and several minor plot twists. This gets a five because I happened to guess a major plot point.<br><br><i># The Witch of Duva</i> - ★★★★★<br>This is one of the best short stories I have ever read. I ended in near tears. It's <i>filled</i> with Leigh Bardugo vibes. You can read this <a href="http://www.tor.com/2012/06/06/the-witch-of-duva-a-ravkan-folk-tale/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>. <br><br><i># The Little Knife</i> - ★★★★★<br>Oh my god this was just beautiful? It's a story about agency, especially of women. And the last illustration is genuinely one of the most beautiful things I've ever seen. <br><br><i># The Soldier Prince</i> - ★★★★☆<br>This story is eerie and heart-tingling and utterly fabulous. I adore how each fairy tale changes in vibe based on what country it originates from; this is a Kerch myth, and you can completely tell. <br><br><i># When Water Sang Fire</i> - ★★★☆☆<br>This was very good, and the artwork - especially the mermaids - was some of my favorite from the whole book. I also love the subversive nature of the retelling. But... idk, I feel somewhat baited? I thought the two girls were a couple for around ten pages when they're in fact just friends. <br><br>VERDICT: What a collection. Highly recommended for anyone who's a fan of the Grisha world.<br><br><br><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/girladamparrish" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14949311118799916139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText13970163991788976628" style="display:none">'tis the season for fairy tales and leigh bardugo is a retelling queen! but honestly, she could write the same word over and over for 100 pages and i would still love it. plus, the illustrations in this are nothing short of remarkable! this is such a treasure of a book!<br /><br />ayama and the thorn wood - ive actually never heard this story before, but its such an beautiful telling and so unique!<br />4.5/5<br /><br />the too clever fox - basically, this makes me wish i was more clever and that the fox was my spirit animal. lol. <br />4.5/5<br /><br />the witch of duva - i really admire the dark spin on this story. its so magically twisted -- perfect for my black heart. <br />3.5/5<br /><br />little knife - awww. so delightful and important. such a lovely story. <br />4/5<br /><br />the soldier prince - ive never really been a fan of the nutcracker, but this gives me all the those winter feels. <br />4/5<br /><br />when water sang fire - yessss. my love, in all his cameo glory! my favourite story only because of the darkling. obvs. <br />5/5<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars overall</i></b></span>

<div id="review_2087083354" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2087083354" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2087083354?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2087083354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2110111240354173673"><b>Who knew that genuine beauty can be found in midnight tales infused with a dash of twisted?</b><br/><blockquote>
  <b>“Bad fates do not always follow those who deserve them.” </b>
</blockquote><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34076952.The_Language_of_Thorns_Midnight_Tales_and_Dangerous_Magic__Grisha_Verse___0_5___2_5___2_6_' title='The Language of Thorns Midnight Tales and Dangerous Magic (Grisha Verse, #0.5, #2.5, #2.6) by Leigh Bardugo' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Language of Thorns: Midnight Tales and Dangerous Magic</a> is a collection of tales inspired by <b>folklore</b> and beloved stories, such as <b>The Little Mermaid</b>, <b>Hansel and Gretel</b> and <b>The Nutcracker</b>, but they follow a different path. Through <b>lush, marvelous illustrations</b> and words that warm your heart only to tear it from your chest, between thorns drawi</span>
  <span id="freeText2110111240354173673" style="display:none"><b>Who knew that genuine beauty can be found in midnight tales infused with a dash of twisted?</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Bad fates do not always follow those who deserve them.” </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34076952.The_Language_of_Thorns_Midnight_Tales_and_Dangerous_Magic__Grisha_Verse___0_5___2_5___2_6_" title="The Language of Thorns Midnight Tales and Dangerous Magic (Grisha Verse, #0.5, #2.5, #2.6) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">The Language of Thorns: Midnight Tales and Dangerous Magic</a> is a collection of tales inspired by <b>folklore</b> and beloved stories, such as <b>The Little Mermaid</b>, <b>Hansel and Gretel</b> and <b>The Nutcracker</b>, but they follow a different path. Through <b>lush, marvelous illustrations</b> and words that warm your heart only to tear it from your chest, between thorns drawing blood entwined with fragnant roses, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4575289.Leigh_Bardugo" title="Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Leigh Bardugo</a> weaves six <b>hauntingly beautiful and disturbing tales</b>, that stir a wave of unease that you cannot quell. You think you know where the story goes, but the ending is always unconventional, and leaves a bitter taste in your mouth; they teach you that, perhaps, you got all the stories wrong. The heroine does not always ride into the sunset on the back of her one true love's steed. Her one true love may be cruel, greedy or manipulative, the ones meant to protect her those who inflict devastating pain, and fairy god-mothers do not save the day. While your hair curls from the steam rising out of the witch's pot, and your fingers grow sticky with the burnt sugar of the candies you savored, you delve into dangerous magic, you're outsmarted by pretty facades and deep down, you're greatful your grandmother did not narrate you those tales when you were only a child, craving adventure and romance, because she would have doomed you into a childhood deprived of sleep. But mind that with her <b>deliciously creepy</b> tales, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4575289.Leigh_Bardugo" title="Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Leigh Bardugo</a> takes you back to Ravka, Fjerda and Kerch, to lands familiar yet peculiar, where you once experienced joy, heartbreak and love.<br>You feel at home.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509306823ra/24308452.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>“This is the problem with making a thing forbidden. It does nothing but build an ache in the heart.” </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Ayama and the Thorn Wood</b> follows a loud but neglected girl and her encounters with a terrible beast, while <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17790188.The_Too_Clever_Fox__Grisha_Verse___2_5_" title="The Too-Clever Fox (Grisha Verse, #2.5) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">The Too-Clever Fox</a> focuses on an ugly but cunning fox trying to outsmart a devious predator. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13643163.The_Witch_of_Duva__Grisha_Verse___0_5_" title="The Witch of Duva (Grisha Verse, #0.5) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">The Witch of Duva</a> is the story of young Nadya, who lives in a vilage near haunted woods, where girls go missing and an evil stepmother drives her to the witch's lair. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20818790.Little_Knife__Grisha_Verse___2_6_" title="Little Knife (Grisha Verse, #2.6) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Knife</a> a poor man tries to win the heart of the duke's beautiful daughter, who doesn't use his wits and courage to pass the trials set but the greedy duke, but calls to magic instead. Only magic has, as always, a price. <b>The Soldier Prince</b> narrates how the creations of a wicked clocksmith came to life and claimed their destiny, and my personal favorite, <b>When Water Sang Fire</b>, goes back in time, when mermaids took human form and sang tempests and storms.<br><blockquote>
  <b>“When no one is looking at you, or whispering to you, who are you then?” </b>
</blockquote><br>A collection of six lavishly illustrated tales that <b>blend folklore with wondrous creativity and a pinch of darkness</b>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34076952.The_Language_of_Thorns_Midnight_Tales_and_Dangerous_Magic__Grisha_Verse___0_5___2_5___2_6_" title="The Language of Thorns Midnight Tales and Dangerous Magic (Grisha Verse, #0.5, #2.5, #2.6) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">The Language of Thorns: Midnight Tales and Dangerous Magic</a> is the perfect read for cold weather and thirsty hearts in search of magic.<br><br> <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/kat/904-thelanguageofthorns" rel="nofollow noopener">Review also posted on BookNest!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2110111240354173673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_2042907422" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2042907422" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2042907422?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=hey-shorty">hey-shorty</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2042907422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12399254559720548525"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best YA fantasy! what will happen?</b><br/><br/>this is gonna be just pure reader response here, with no attempt made towards any objective assessment or critical analysis. when it comes to bardugo’s fairy tales, i’m just a box full of puppies and all i can do is grin. <br/><br/>i’d read three of these stories before this collection was published, as free tor shorts. i reviewed ‘em here, if you really do need to have your critical analysis beast fed, or if you just want th</span>
  <span id="freeText12399254559720548525" style="display:none"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best YA fantasy! what will happen?</b><br><br>this is gonna be just pure reader response here, with no attempt made towards any objective assessment or critical analysis. when it comes to bardugo’s fairy tales, i’m just a box full of puppies and all i can do is grin. <br><br>i’d read three of these stories before this collection was published, as free tor shorts. i reviewed ‘em here, if you really do need to have your critical analysis beast fed, or if you just want the links to where you can read the stories for free:<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/966473987" rel="nofollow noopener">The Too-Clever Fox</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/971138700" rel="nofollow noopener">The Witch of Duva</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/978759105" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Knife</a><br><br>even though i’ve read dozens more since then, those three stories are still top-ranked in my “free tor short hall of fame.” they are the perfect kind of fairytale - not cheesy or gentle, not dark and edgy just to shock or subvert, but … honest. they are as close to feeling “real” as a fairytale can get, in their beating hearts and blood beneath the magic. coming across them, i felt like i’d discovered something exquisite - it felt like a gift, like pure magic and wonder handcrafted for me. and when i heard this was going to be published and realized i’d already read half of the book, it is a testament to just how good those stories are that i didn’t feel a scrap of disappointment. i only felt, “oh, good - now they can truly be mine, away from my computer.” <br><br>and now they are. the three stories i hadn’t read were every bit as good as the ones i had, and the artwork - it’s phenomenal. as each story progresses, it grows its own illustrated borders page by page simultaneously across the verso/recto, until the images connect triumphantly, or devastatingly, followed by a single, full-page illustration serving as an explosive “THE END.” the illustrations are quite cheeky in their details, too, which makes them perfect companions to these little story bombs.<br><br>she’s so good at these that as much as i enjoy her longer books, if she decided to devote herself entirely to fleshing out her imaginary lands through folklore like this, i would applaud her choices without reservation. <br><br>maybe i will write more at a later date, but for now, just this happy cheer.<br><br>also, i'm really glad i have a signed copy, otherwise this page would feel like it was missing something<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley003/IMG_5175_zpswcirmi4b.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507472667i/24119011._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_5175_zpswcirmi4b.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>***********************************************<br><br>five perfect perfect perfect stars. review to come, but for now - much swooning delight.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>

<div id="review_2097670853" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2097670853" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2097670853?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250173928" href="/book/show/35094043-the-language-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2097670853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16375103982402574816"><i>”Bad fates do not always follow those who deserve them.”</i><br/><br/>I guess that’s a wisdom that sets the tone for this entire collection of dark fairy tales. If there is a recurrent theme that runs through all of those stories then it’s the fact that the bad guys don’t always get what they deserve. Which, quite honestly, made this even more intriguing for me. So what else did I love about Leigh’s stories? That they were as dark as the midnight hour. *lol* I mean if you’re familiar with fairy tales you know</span>
  <span id="freeText16375103982402574816" style="display:none"><i>”Bad fates do not always follow those who deserve them.”</i><br /><br />I guess that’s a wisdom that sets the tone for this entire collection of dark fairy tales. If there is a recurrent theme that runs through all of those stories then it’s the fact that the bad guys don’t always get what they deserve. Which, quite honestly, made this even more intriguing for me. So what else did I love about Leigh’s stories? That they were as dark as the midnight hour. *lol* I mean if you’re familiar with fairy tales you know that all of them have a lesson you’re supposed to learn and that they are pretty cruel and wicked as well. So in that regard Leigh certainly delivered. XD Some of those stories gave me goose bumps and caused me to shake my head in disgust. And others made me wonder how different the story could have ended if the characters would have been a little bit more on guard. No matter the outcome of the stories they were all amazing though. As were the drawings around the pages! I loved them so much! There were so many little details and each and every single story turned out to be a flip book when you went through it fast enough. If you ask me a lot of thought went into this book and I really appreciated it. <br /><br />This said let’s take a short look at the six stories themselves: <br /><br /><b>Ayama and the Thorn Wood:</b> 4/5<br /><br /><i>”Then perhaps you might show mercy freely?”<br />“My father never taught me mercy.”<br />“And can you not learn?”</i> <br /><br />I really enjoyed that one even though it kind of reminded me of a combination of <b>“The Beauty and the Beast”</b> and <b>“Arabian Nights”</b>. Well, if the beauty would have been a plain girl instead of a beauty and if the stories wouldn’t have had an ending. *lol* <br /><br /><b>The Too-Clever Fox:</b> 5/5<br /><br /><i>”If you like, you may have me as supper. I warn you, though, I am stringy and tough. Only my tongue holds savor. I make a bitter meal, but excellent company.”</i><br /><br />Ahh I really loved that one!! Okay, I might be biased because I love foxes and cunning people/creatures but Koja was awesome! How he got out of the most delicate situations was great and that fox had all my respect! &lt;3 <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i>”The trap is loneliness, and none of us escape it. Not even me.”</i> <br />I KNEW it was Sofiya all along! That woman might have been a good actress but I wasn’t fooled by her! Still when she started to peel Koja’s pelt I felt sick to my stomach and I was so glad that someone heard his screams! Poor Koja. I’m sure he never trusted a human being ever again. &gt;_&lt;  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>The Witch of Duva:</b> 5/5<br /><br /><i>”What is it you want?”<br />“I want to go home,” said Nadya. <br />“Well then,” said Magda. “You’d better start shoveling.”</i><br /><br />This was a totally unique story and I never heard anything like it before. It plays with how people perceive others and it shows that you should never give into your prejudices. I really loved that one and the moral of the story was driven home with quite a punch. XD <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Well, this was another story that made me feel sick. I never expected Nadya’s father to be the beast and to witness how he ate and savoured the gingerbread Nadya. *shudders*Turns out her mean stepmother actually saved her from her own father. Perceptions! *shakes head* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Little Knife:</b> 3/5<br /><br /><i>”Papa forgive me, but what way is this to find a husband? Soon I will have a fine mirror, but will I have good man?”</i><br /><br />For some reason this was the story I enjoyed least. I don’t know why but maybe because it wasn’t all too shocking? I mean there is definitely a lesson to be learned and Semyon’s relationship as a tidemaker with the river was interesting, but the ending... I dunno. *shrugs* Maybe I didn’t like the fact that the beautiful girl always obeyed her father’s wishes. *lol*<br /><br /><b>The Soldier Prince:</b> 4,5/5<br /><br /><i>”Are you mine?”</i><br /><br />Okay! For me that one was super creepy because I’m kind of afraid of dolls and clowns. You might call it a mild coulrophobia and automatonophobia? &gt;_&lt; They just scare the bejesus out of me. (I know why I never read “It”.) So this story was kinda tough to read and gave me all sorts of anxiety. I somehow managed to get through it though and I’m glad I survived it. I have absolutely no idea how Clara and Frederik could play with the Soldier Prince, let alone love him, but oh well. Still, that ending... *shudders and hides under a blanket*<br /><br /><b>When Water sang Fire:</b> 3,5/5<br /><br /><i>”Magic doesn’t require beauty,” she said. “Easy magic is pretty. Great magic asks that you trouble the waters. It requires a disruption, something new.”</i><br /><br />I think we can all agree that this was some sort of “The Little Mermaid” retelling and the longest story out of those six. The relationship between Ulla and Signy was really interesting but if you ask me it was only friendship. I know some people thought they might have a relationship but I doubt it. They both just loved to sing and were connected through their magic and their love for music. The ending didn’t really surprise me and Roffe’s character and his intentions were obvious right from the start. The most interesting piece here was probably the apprentice, which apparently was the Darkling?! I dunno. He was a too little part of this story to actually make assumptions. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[If the apprentice was the Darkling then this would mean Ulla is his sister. So he’s related to a sea witch? And what about his mother?! I don’t see the connections here, but oh well, might be just me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />This was the perfect Halloween read and if you love creepy and dark fairy tales this is definitely your kind of book! The cover, the illustrations and the flip book element only made this even more enjoyable and every time I picked up “The Language of Thorns” I had a smile on my face. I just loved to hold this in my hands! If you want to read those stories properly, I’d recommend going for a physical copy. You won’t regret it. ;-)<br /><br />____________________________________<br /><br />This was just great! &lt;3<br />I loved all of those fairy tales. Some more than others but in general they were all amazing! =)<br />What I really liked was that they were so dark and creepy! Ahhh! I enjoyed this so much!<br />Perfect read for October! <br /><br />Full RTC soon! Stay tuned! ;-)<br />____________________________________<br /><br />It’s getting dark and cold outside which means it’s the perfect time to read fairy tales!<br />Dark fairy tales!! <br />Leigh Bardugo fairy tales! *lol*<br /><br />Which means I’m finally picking this up! =)<br />I can’t wait to dive into this book, especially because it’s so damn pretty.<br />Love the cover and the pictures on the pages. Somebody thought long and hard when she/he made those drawings!! &lt;33<br /><br />Leigh’s stories in combination with the beautiful art will be a treat! XD</span>
  <a data-text-id="16375103982402574816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
