<div id="review_1897494423" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1897494423" />
    <a title="Cesar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34467577-cesar"><img alt="Cesar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501005350p2/34467577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1897494423?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cesar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cesar" href="/user/show/34467577-cesar">Cesar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1897494423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3527974213444086772">10 trillion stars/5<br/><br/><i>“This is the problem with making a thing forbidden. It does nothing but build an ache in the heart.”</i><br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506639079i/24035430._SY540_.jpg' width='520' height='446' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Words cannot even begin to describe how much I loved <b>The Language of Thorns</b>. I am trying to find the right words but I can't. The best way to express my love is through this gif.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475082067ra/20679219.gif' width='400' height='226' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In all seriousness though, I really loved this book. Everything about this book, from the words to the drawings to the stories is just stunning and beautiful and breathtaking and every other synonym th</span>
  <span id="freeText3527974213444086772" style="display:none">10 trillion stars/5<br><br><i>“This is the problem with making a thing forbidden. It does nothing but build an ache in the heart.”</i><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506639079i/24035430._SY540_.jpg" width="520" height="446" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Words cannot even begin to describe how much I loved <b>The Language of Thorns</b>. I am trying to find the right words but I can't. The best way to express my love is through this gif.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475082067ra/20679219.gif" width="400" height="226" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In all seriousness though, I really loved this book. Everything about this book, from the words to the drawings to the stories is just stunning and beautiful and breathtaking and every other synonym that is related to beautiful. <b>It was that good.</b> I have admired Leigh's writing style before, but this one takes the cake with cherries on top. It really felt like I was reading actual fairy tales. <br><br>The Language of Thorns takes inspiration from different fairy tales and Leigh tells them in such a unique way so that it belongs to the Grishaverse. You got ones that are like <i>Hansel and Gretel, Beauty and the Beast</i>, and the <i>Little Mermaid</i>. Except imagine them dark, twisted, and beautiful. My kind of fairytales. And yes, I know the original fairytales were dark, but Leigh does it in a way that makes them even more unique.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394051576ra/8801440.gif" width="341" height="276" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>In the book, there are 3 new stories and 3 other ones that were originally in e-book format. Those are: The Too-Clever Fox, The Witch of Duva, and Little Knife. I have not read them but now I'm glad they were in this book.<br><br>These stories are not what they appear at first glance. I knew I was in for some dark and twisted stuff since the tales are from the Grishaverse. Even still, I was surprised by the stories and the characters because I am not kidding when I say the stories are dark. No rainbows, puppies, and sunshine in this book, kiddos.<br><br>If I had to choose a favorite story, it would have to be <b>When Water Sang Fire</b>. I loved that story mainly because of the characters, the lyrical writing, how Leigh takes mermaids/sirens and turns it into something different. <br>(It also helped that I was listening to <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FwhU08XH-kA" rel="nofollow noopener">This</a> because of the whole siren aspect of it.)<br><br>And, a certain <b>dark</b> character appears.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506625167ra/24033559.gif" width="214" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(Hello Darkling. 😙 *proceeds to make out with the Darkling*)<br><br>I really don't have anything negative to say about the stories. Yeah, some of them can be long, but the stories help with the pacing, especially if you really like the writing and the stories. <br><br>I just love everything about the Grishaverse. And, it was recently announced that Leigh is coming back to the Grishaverse with a duology that is centered around Nikolai!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/655328.gif" width="250" height="187" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Verdict</u>
</b><br><br>I absolutely loved this book. Everything about it was lovely. I highly recommend this if you really are a fan of the Grishaverse or just like fairytales.<br><br>Thanks for reading my review!<br><br>-Cesar</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2255625031" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2255625031" />
    <a title="Shruti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67778438-shruti"><img alt="Shruti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563992774p2/67778438.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2255625031?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shruti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shruti" href="/user/show/67778438-shruti">Shruti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67778438-shruti?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67778438-shruti?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2255625031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11895432940767270573"><b>
  <i>“You see, some people are born with a piece of night inside, and that hollow place can never be filled – not with all the good food or sunshine in the world. That emptiness cannot be banished, and so some days we wake with the feeling of the wind blowing through, and we must simply endure it as the boy did.” </i>
</b><br/><br/>Beautiful. Haunting. Intriguing. <br/><br/>Bardugo can create such magic with her beautiful writing! This was exactly what I needed to restore my love for Bardugo's writing after I was disappointe</span>
  <span id="freeText11895432940767270573" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“You see, some people are born with a piece of night inside, and that hollow place can never be filled – not with all the good food or sunshine in the world. That emptiness cannot be banished, and so some days we wake with the feeling of the wind blowing through, and we must simply endure it as the boy did.” </i>
</b><br><br>Beautiful. Haunting. Intriguing. <br><br>Bardugo can create such magic with her beautiful writing! This was exactly what I needed to restore my love for Bardugo's writing after I was disappointed in <i>Shadow and Bone</i>. This book is a collection of six fairytale-like illustrated stories set in the Grishaverse. <br><br>The highlights of these short stories are :<br><br> 1. Reimagined fairytale retellings with dark themes<br> 2. Unexpected plot twists<br> 3. Stunning illustrations <br> <br>This collection features the different worlds that Bardugo creates, and these stories are filled with creepiness and intrigue. Each story conveys different messages which is totally different from the actual fairytales. Throughout the whole book, I was either mesmerized by Bardugo’s magical writing style, in awe of illustrations or just waiting to see what would happen next.<i>The Language of Thorns</i> is just an all-around beautiful book.<br><br>It is not necessary to read any of the Grishaverse books beforehand, although I think the tales will be more fun that way.<br><br><br>¤ <b>Ayama and The Thorn Wood</b> ⭐⭐⭐⭐. 5<br><br><b>
  <i>“This goes to show you that sometimes the unseen is not to be feared and that those meant to love us most are not always the ones who do.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514094640i/24749771._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This story is from Zemeni and is retelling of a sort of mix between <i> Cinderella</i> and <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>, about a strong hearted ordinary girl and a beastly prince. This story breaks the stereotype of having a beautiful or handsome character as the main character of fairytales. I also loved how the characters in the story also told stories, so the book-within-a-book feeling was strong here. It was my second favourite in the collection. <br><br><br>¤ <b>The Too-clever Fox</b> ⭐⭐⭐. 5<br><br><b>
  <i>“A lesser creature might have closed his eyes and prayed for nothing more than a quick death. But if Koja had words, then he had hope.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514094639i/24749769._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It is a Ravkan tale about a little fox Koja who uses his wits to get him out of some dangerous situations. This almost has the feeling of a fable. There wasn’t as many twists in this story as in the previous one, the ending was still surprising. <br><br>P.S Bardugo confirmed that this story is our very own witty thief Kaz’s favourite!!!! &lt;3 <br><br><br>¤ <b> The Witch of Duva</b> ⭐⭐⭐⭐<br><br><b>
  <i>“Dark things have a way of slipping in through narrow spaces.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514094639i/24749768._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I think the idea for this Ravkan tale came from <i>Hansel and Gretel</i>.It follows Nadya as she finds out the secret of how girls went missing in Duva. The story definitely was the most disturbing and creepy ones for me. The ending has a big twist that I did not see coming a mile away, and it just made the story all that much better.<br><br><br>¤ <b>The Little Knife</b> ⭐⭐⭐. 5<br><br><b><i>“She never worried when her beauty faded, for in her reflection she always saw a free woman.”</i> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514094640i/24749772._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>This Ravkan tale gathers all of the familiar elements from many old fairy tales: a competition for the hand of a beautiful maiden and a trio of impossible tasks .In this story, Grisha power of a Tidemaker was mentioned and used. It’s a good story with more lesson,like Too Clever Fox. Still it managed to surprise me at the ending like all the others. <br><br><br>¤ <b>The Soldier Prince </b>⭐⭐⭐<br><br><b>
  <i>“Who are you when no one picks you up to hold you?” asked the Rat King. “When no one is looking at you, or whispering to you, who are you then?" </i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514094639i/24749770._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>This Kerch tale is a reimagined <i>The Nutcracker</i> retelling with Grisha Fabrikator magic and the spirit of a toy which comes alive. This was all about self-discovery and knowing the importance of making our own story. But I felt that the ending was very eerie and unsettling. <br><br><br>¤ <b>When Water Sang Fire</b> ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐<br><br><b>
  <i>“This is the problem with making a thing forbidden. It does nothing but build an ache in the heart.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514094639i/24749767._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This Fjerdan story is a retelling of <i>The little mermaid</i>, about a sildroher mermaid named Ulla who dreams of being able to use her singing magic as she chooses.It poses questions on the cost of magic, the sacrifices we make for our ambitions, and the price we pay to earn social acceptance. I loved every moment of this story and it was my most favorite from the whole collection.This was no doubt the perfect strong story to end the book. <br><br>P.S The Darkling made an appearance in this story!!<br><i>"The boy’s clothes were black, his hair blacker still, and he was looking directly at Ulla, the weight of his stare heavy ballast." </i><br><br><br><br>Overall there wasn’t a single story in this book that I didn’t liked or enjoyed reading. Every fairytale was just so well-thought-out. It is a treat for all the Bardugo fans. Even if you haven’t read any Bardugo books yet and if you're interested in dark twists in fairytales, then this one is perfect for you!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11895432940767270573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2137536283" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2137536283" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487160141p2/8836060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2137536283?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8836060-michelle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8836060-michelle?shelf=grishaverse">grishaverse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2137536283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer476153221573863749">I just love the Grisha Trilogy, and “The Language of Thorns” is the icing on the cake. These six original stories are broken up into different regions: with three stories coming from Ravka, and the rest from Novyi Zem, Kerch, and Fjerda. Those who have not read Leigh Bardugo’s work are not necessarily required to read her previous novels to understand the stories. They can be enjoyed as simply that: stories.<br/><br/>Bardugo has nailed the fireside tale telling feel -- it’s like you can feel the warmth of</span>
  <span id="freeText476153221573863749" style="display:none">I just love the Grisha Trilogy, and “The Language of Thorns” is the icing on the cake. These six original stories are broken up into different regions: with three stories coming from Ravka, and the rest from Novyi Zem, Kerch, and Fjerda. Those who have not read Leigh Bardugo’s work are not necessarily required to read her previous novels to understand the stories. They can be enjoyed as simply that: stories.<br /><br />Bardugo has nailed the fireside tale telling feel -- it’s like you can feel the warmth of the fire on your face, the cold nipping the back of your ears, and see her face lit up by the flames as she regales you with dark tales at midnight.<br /><br /><b>“Ayama and the Thorn Wood”</b> is a really enjoyable tone-setter for the series, getting you into the voice, style, and tone of the collection, all the while telling a story of bravery. <br /><br /><b>“The Too-Clever Fox”</b> is a fun story with a pretty gnarly climax. I didn’t guess the plot twist until it was too late, and there were a couple of moments where my skin crawled. <br /><br /><b>“The Witch of Duva”</b> felt the closest to the fairy tales I remember from my childhood, but Bardugo, as she does so well in this collection, writes an excellent twist. This is one of my favorites.<br /><br />As expected, <b>“Little Knife” </b>had a wonderful twist I didn’t see coming. There is a very strong message in this tale that I enjoyed reading immensely. This story is gorgeous.<br /><br /><b>“The Soldier Prince”</b> is a pretty haunting and odd tale that built its momentum from about half-way after being a bit of a slow starter. Bardugo has done a magnificent job of creating a magical mystery as the nutcracker tries to work out what he is, his reality, and what he wants in life.<br /><br /><b>“When Water Sang Fire”</b> is a novella that had my least favorite start to any entry in this collection, but became the best story in the book -- hands down! This story drew out a lot of emotions from me: I felt joy, sadness, anger, and a need for revenge. It was a perfect way to finish the collection -- a tale of friendship and of being different, and of loyalty and betrayal. I need a sequel for this!<br /><br />Each tale is as mesmerizing as it is enjoyable and, combined with Sara Kipin’s illustrations, “The Language of Thorns” achieves a storybook quality. Every illustration draws out more curious details that fill up the border of each page as the story progresses. When the story is complete, readers are given a full double-spread of artwork to accompany the tale.<br /><br />These stories offer no simple architecture of good and evil, but force you to live inside their clockworks -- fear and desire twisted together into that ideal mix that speaks both to children, intimating that the world isn't all pastels and candy, and adults who already know its dangers far too well. These tales are the epitome of brutal honesty and distorted reality.<br /><br /><i>“Love speaks in flowers. Truth requires thorns.” </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="476153221573863749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1897920908" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1897920908" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1897920908?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=taylor-swift-like-prose">taylor-swift-like-prose</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=my-inner-feminist-cries-with-joy">my-inner-feminist-cries-with-joy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=fabulous-five-stars">fabulous-five-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1897920908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12131587851495202768"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"In the year that summer stayed too long, the heat lay upon the prairie with the weight of a corpse."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Can we please talk about what a <b>goddamn gift of a writer Leigh is?</b> Beautiful writing, to me, isn't how many constellations you can find in a love interest's freckles, or stringing together a tinsel chain of adjectives, but the ability to reinvent words. Look at that sentence. It captures the fly-buzzing, desolate atmosphere perfectly while lending a new dimension to the word corpse.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444234335ra/16472947.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>T</span>
  <span id="freeText12131587851495202768" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"In the year that summer stayed too long, the heat lay upon the prairie with the weight of a corpse."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Can we please talk about what a <b>goddamn gift of a writer Leigh is?</b> Beautiful writing, to me, isn't how many constellations you can find in a love interest's freckles, or stringing together a tinsel chain of adjectives, but the ability to reinvent words. Look at that sentence. It captures the fly-buzzing, desolate atmosphere perfectly while lending a new dimension to the word corpse.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444234335ra/16472947.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>These stories are <b>lush, thorny creatures.</b> Each and every one of them comes with a twist. They challenge traditional fairy tales through modern morals and values—wicked sisters may not always be what they see, magic might not always follow rules. <br><br>There's very little I can say without coming off as cheap or sentimental. The Language of Thorns is a work best experienced. <br><br>So instead <b>I'm going to give out awards.</b><br><br><b>The Creepy AF Award</b> goes to the Kerch tale The Soldier Prince. Primarily a Nutcracker retelling, all I can say is, if this what Kaz and everyone in Ketterdam grew up listening to, no wonder they turned out to be morally deficient, gun-wielding gangsters.<br><br><b>Mother's Favorite </b>goes to the Zemini-originated Ayama and the Thorn Wood. Reason? We get an extra three stories sealed in one because Ayama takes the One Thousand &amp; Nights road in beast-slaying. <br><br>The coveted <b>Fan-Voted Award</b> goes to When Water Sang Fire from Fjerda. Not a spoiler, Bardugo mentioned on social media a known character would make an appearance and posted a fairly obvious excerpt. (No, I won't tell you who is) <br><br>Me, personally, didn't enjoy it as much because it shared a bit too many similarities to Marissa Meyer's the Little Mermaid retelling from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31450752.Because_You_Love_to_Hate_Me_13_Tales_of_Villainy" title="Because You Love to Hate Me 13 Tales of Villainy by Ameriie" rel="nofollow noopener">Because You Love to Hate Me: 13 Tales of Villainy</a>. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It ruined the ending for me <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> However, the plot of When Water Sang Fire is far superior, as are the writing and characters. <br><br>As for our returning champions, Ravkan folklore which had been published online for free before this collection, I present...<br><br><b>A Tale Worthy of Kaz and Inej</b> to The Too-Clever Fox. Fyi, Bardugo said this would be Kaz's favorite fairy tale. <br><br><b>A Darker Version of Hansel and Gretel If That's Even Possible Award</b> goes to The Witch of Duva. Helpful warning not to read this over milk and cookies.<br><br>And finally, for The Little Knife, the <b>Hufflepuff Award</b> because it's equally brilliant and Helga Hufflepuff is an equal opportunist. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"But as you leave that dark gap in the trees behind, remember that to use a thing is not to own it. And should you ever take a bride, listen closely to her questions. In them you may hear her true name like the thunder of a lost river, like the sighing of the sea."</i>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12131587851495202768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3k6SiQek3g7KkCF7CuJ/Wg80/XFiJElvlq91E1NCh4/7zqFdiLJB4j1rJ6zhh+Y+34WAXh9AccGSbZxB06lpkA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QZ3jVO73D4bSPvn8HUC7os2O4ovFP8kWEVAzMnYpUctkHdCAYeGQaiXF/yv2JSLGHT+fpLhb8bgVktpg9sK/1A==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer8646940512577069760">Leigh Bardugo is a #1 New York Times bestselling author of fantasy novels and the creator of the Grishaverse (coming soon to Netflix) which spans the Shadow and Bone Trilogy, the Six of Crows Duology, The Language of Thorns, and King of Scars— with more to come. Her short stories can be found in multiple anthologies, including the Best American Science Fiction & Fantasy. Her other works include Wo</span>
  <span id="freeText8646940512577069760" style="display:none">Leigh Bardugo is a #1 New York Times bestselling author of fantasy novels and the creator of the Grishaverse (coming soon to Netflix) which spans the Shadow and Bone Trilogy, the Six of Crows Duology, The Language of Thorns, and King of Scars— with more to come. Her short stories can be found in multiple anthologies, including the Best American Science Fiction &amp; Fantasy. Her other works include Wonder Woman: Warbringer and Ninth House (Goodreads Choice Winner for Best Fantasy 2019) which is being developed for television by Amazon Studios. Leigh was born in Jerusalem, grew up in Southern California, and graduated from Yale University. These days she lives and writes in Los Angeles. For information on new releases and appearances, sign up for her <a href="https://https//leighbardugo.us11.list-manage.com/subscribe?u=160b0462d4826c60dbb8af320&amp;id=ec014907b2" rel="nofollow noopener">newsletter</a>.<br /><br />She would be delighted if you followed her on <a href="http://twitter.com/Lbardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>, elated if you visited her at <a href="http://leighbardugo.com" rel="nofollow noopener">LeighBardugo.com</a>, and fairly giddy if you liked her selfies on <a href="http://instagram.com/lbardugo/7" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a>. <br /><br /></span>
